<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>In recent years, there has been a rapid growth in the development of RFID systems for use in various industrial fields. For RFID systems operating at LF and HF frequencies, information and power transmission are generally based on the coupling inductance, while for UHF and microwave frequencies, the communication between the reader and the tag is based on the electromagnetic wave propagation. The two most important parts of an RFID system are the transponder (antenna) and the reader. When designing the reader, a compact-size antenna is of paramount importance <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>.</p><p>An extensive research and development has been done to improve the antennas for the RFID applications. A compact dual linearly polarized aperture-coupled microstrip patch antenna array system has been introduced in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a> for such applications. A printed Yagi antenna has been introduced in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a> to increase the gain and the front-to-back ratio of the tag's antenna and extend the reading range. Printed loop antenna for near-field RFID readers is another option that has been introduced in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>. There are a few articles that use printed dipole as RFID antennas.</p><p>Most of these reported antennas occupy a large substrate surface area, and a challenging problem for the designers is to reduce the size of the overall antenna. For this purpose, the folded printed dipole antenna with two radiating arms and a shorting strip is proposed in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>. Each radiating arm is bent into a G-shape to obtain a compact size. Also, the step impedance transmission lines have been used in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a> to make the dipole antenna even more compact. Efficient planar left-handed antenna working in the zero-order mode is another way to reduce the dimensions of the antenna. This approach takes advantage of the left-handed topology to achieve well-matched input impedance values and a miniaturized antenna, with improved performances with respect to the conventional left-handed loading <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>. The meander-line approach has been used in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a> to design compact RFID tag antennas. Such antennas have inductive input impedance that can be complex-conjugate-matched with the tag chips and, as such, are more suitable for tag antennas. However, due to the real part of the input impedance being low, these antennas have low efficiencies.</p><p>Recently, we used a planar artificial transmission line loading with single-layer printed circuit broad fabrication process for miniaturization of a quasi-Yagi antenna <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a>. Here, this technique is considered in more detail and discussion. In this method, a compact omnidirectional printed quasi-Yagi antenna loaded by artificial transmission line (ATL) structure has been introduced to reduce the overall dimension of the printed antenna suitable for RFID applications. In the proposed antenna, a new microstrip artificial transmission line that is based on the ATL given in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_1">[13]</a> has been used for loading the radiating arms of the quasi-Yagi antenna. This new artificial transmission line composed of microstrip quasi-lumped elements and their discontinuities is able to synthesize transmission lines with a wide range of characteristic impedances and electrical lengths and may therefore significantly reduce the required physical lengths of both high- and low-impedance lines. Since the proposed antenna has an impedance of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 7.09em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.369em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1006.31em 2.526em -999.997em); vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/002E.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 3px; height: 2px; height: 11px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-7" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/00A0.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 0px; height: 0px; margin-right: 0.243em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-8" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/03A9.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 11px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">46.66-j4.27\ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, it is more suitable for reader antennas, and because of its excellent efficiency, it can give a great read range in comparison to previous work. The proposed antenna is fabricated and tested, and results are compared to those of the simulation. Simulated results are obtained through the commercially available software package HFSS.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Artificial Transmission Line</h2></div><p>A simple antenna suitable for RFID application is the printed dipole antenna. The physical length of each arm of a dipole antenna is approximately <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-9" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 2.105em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.865em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.87em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-10" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-11" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-12" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BB.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-13" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-14" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-15" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0067.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 7px; vertical-align: -2px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-16" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-17" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-18" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/002F.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 16px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-19" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0034.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">\lambda_{\rm g}/4</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and the electrical length is 90Â°. In most RFID applications, this length is very large, especially in the UHF zone. Generally, this is considered as a big drawback. To overcome this obstacle, an ATL structure is proposed here.</p><p>The miniaturization of passive microwave components by means of ATL structures has drawn more and more attention recently <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_2">[13]</a>. To reduce the physical length of a microstrip line while maintaining exactly the same electrical length as the conventional counterpart, a planar ATL can be incorporated. The planar artificial transmission line is composed of quasi-lumped elements that can be replaced by standard discontinuous lines such as meandered and interdigital lines. To the knowledge of the present authors, up until now, the ATL structures reported in the literature have been used to reduce the size of microwave components. In this letter, we use the ATL structure to reduce the size of the required printed antenna for the RFID applications.</p><p>The ATL structure can be applied to the arms of a simple printed dipole antenna. However, to be able to apply this, the width of the arms should be large enough in order for the ATLs to be included. Thus, first a hypothetical rectangular patch can replace the open-ended transmission line of each dipole arm. Then, the ATL is incorporated within each of the two patches.</p><p>The hypothetical patch is designed to operate at the required frequency of 915 MHz. The equivalent lumped element model of the patch antenna is a parallel <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-20" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.565em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.38em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-21" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-22" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/004C.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 10px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-23" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0043.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 12px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">LC</script></tex-math></inline-formula> circuit. The equivalent lumped element model can be turned into an easily realizable printed ATL structure.</p><p>The characteristic impedance of a transmission line is the square root of the equivalent inductance over equivalent capacitance, and also its guided wavenumber is the square root of the equivalent inductance times the capacitance. By increasing the equivalent inductance and capacitance, the guided wavenumber can be increased efficiently to achieve the required electrical length with unchanged characteristic impedance for the line. Thus, the propagation constant can be controlled in an ATL structure, leading to reduced antenna size.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a> shows the structure of the proposed ATL structure (with discontinuities on one side, and a finite ground on the other side of the substrate) replacing the patch in each arm of the original dipole antenna. The structure is fed through a printed transmission line followed by the meander line that is terminated in a narrow rectangular patch. This wide patch provides better radiation efficiency for the cell. Two narrow rectangular patches are also placed on the top and bottom part of the cell in which interdigital lines are created.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6482586/6482586-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6482586/6482586-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 1. </b><fig><p>Structure of the proposed unit-cell printed artificial transmission line.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6482586/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2</a> presents the equivalent lumped-element model of the structure in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a>. The relevant inductances and capacitances, tabulated in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a>, can be obtained through simulation via HFSS package. margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-534" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0029.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 16px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-15">(\beta_{\rm g})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the unit cell of an artificial transmission line can be obtained from <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn1-2" href="#deqn1-2" class="fulltext-link">(1)</a>â<a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn3-4" href="#deqn3-4" class="fulltext-link">(4)</a> while keeping the overall length of the ATL structure much lower than the original printed line. The amount of reduction also depends on the efficiency required for the structure.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Antenna Design and Configuration</h2></div><p>The proposed quasi-Yagi antenna suitable for the RFID application is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 3</a>. For a simple balanced feed, the two radiating arms consisting of ATL cells are connected to a microstrip feedline. To have the phase reversal between the two arms, as required for the dipole, the two ATL structures are placed in reverse. A truncated ground acting as a reflector for the antenna structure is also placed at the bottom of the board.

A prototype of the antenna is fabricated and shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 3(b)</a>. In <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ II</a>, the proposed antenna is compared to some other RFID antennas obtainable in the literature. It can be seen that the proposed antenna has a very compact dimension compared to the others.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Results</h2></div><p>The measured and simulated reflection coefficient of the proposed antenna is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a>. From these results, it can be seen that the antenna resonates at 915 MHz, and good impedance match is achieved. The measured and simulated co- and cross polarization of the E- and H-plane patterns of the proposed antenna are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 5</a> at 915 MHz. As can be seen, the antenna has an omnidirectional pattern in the elevation direction (H-plane), and overall, the cross-polarization level is about 15 dB below the copolarization level. These features make the antenna useful for RFID application.</p><p>In addition, the effect of each of the parameters in the ATL cell shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a> can be studied through simulation. As an example, the effects of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-44-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-724" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.144em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.02em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-725" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-726" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0053.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 10px; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-727" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0034.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-44">S4</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-45-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-728" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.264em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1001.08em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-729" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-730" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0077.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 11px; height: 7px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-731" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0032.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-45">w2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> that are related to the meander-line inductors are demonstrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6</a>. By decreasing <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-46-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-732" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.144em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.02em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-733" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-734" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0053.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 10px; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-735" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0034.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-46">S4</script></tex-math></inline-formula> from 0.3 to 0.18 mm, the overall length of the meandered line decreases, leading to reduced total inductance. This change in the total inductance of the cell reduces the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-47-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-736" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 2.345em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.11em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-737" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-738" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.6em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-739" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/004C.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 10px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-740" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-741" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-742" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0041.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 8px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-743" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0054.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 8px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-744" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/004C.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 8px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.003em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-47">L_{\rm ATL}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn3-4" href="#deqn3-4" class="fulltext-link">(3)</a> and thus shifts the resonance frequency. Similarly, reducing the value of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-48-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-745" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.264em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1001.08em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-746" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-747" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0077.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 11px; height: 7px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-748" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0032.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-48">w2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> shifts the resonance frequency upward.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6482586/6482586-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6482586/6482586-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 6. </b><fig><p>Simulated reflection coefficient of antenna for various design parameters. <i>(top)</i> <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-49-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-749" role="math" style="display: inline-block; <p></p><p>Other parameters of the proposed ATL structure have also been investigated. For example, by increasing <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-51-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-757" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.264em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1001.08em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-758" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-759" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0077.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 11px; height: 7px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-760" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0031.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 10px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-51">w1</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the overall area of the corner patches increases leading to increased total capacitance. The parameter <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-52-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-761" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.844em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.72em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-762" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-763" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/006C.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 4px; height: 12px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-764" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0034.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-52">l4</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is used for adequate adjustment of the phase. By increasing <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-53-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-765" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.204em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.02em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-766" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-767" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0053.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 10px; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-768" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0031.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 10px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-53">S1</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the parasitic capacitance of the meandered line increases, and this leads to enlarged total capacitance.</p><p>In practical situations, it is usual to place such an antenna within some protective covers. It can be shown that if dielectric protective covers are placed on both sides of the proposed antenna, the resonant frequency of the antenna shifts downward, while its pattern changes insignificantly.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>A new ATL structure has been proposed to compact the arms of a quasi-Yagi antenna suitable for RFID readers. The presence of the ATL structure results in reduction of the quasi-Yagi antenna arm's length from the conventional value of 0.25 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-54-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-769" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.084em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.96em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-770" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-771" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-772" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BB.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-773" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-774" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-775" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0067.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 7px; vertical-align: -2px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.203em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-54">\lambda_{\rm g}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to present 0.1 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-55-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-776" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.084em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.96em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-777" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-778" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-779" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BB.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-780" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-781" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-782" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0067.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 7px; vertical-align: -2px; The overall antenna dimension is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-56-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-783" role="math" style="display: inline-block; <script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

		}
	}
});

</script>
